</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Decentralized digital cryptocurrency</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the colloquial expression for coinage, see <a href="/wiki/Bit_(money)" title="Bit (money)">Bit (money)</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"₿" redirects here. Not to be confused with "฿" for <a href="/wiki/Thai_baht" title="Thai baht">Thai baht</a>.</div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1314755338">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:var(--background-color-interactive-subtle,#f8f9fa);color:inherit;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .infobox .side-box{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1;min-width:0}}@media(min-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1092331828">@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .contains-special-characters{width:22em}}</style><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right contains-special-characters noprint selfref"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">special characters</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>.</div></div>
</div>
<p><b>Bitcoin</b> (abbreviation: <b>BTC</b>; <a href="/wiki/Currency_symbol" title="Currency symbol">sign</a>: <b>₿</b>) is the first <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_application" title="Decentralized application">decentralized</a> <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency" title="Cryptocurrency">cryptocurrency</a>. Based on a <a href="/wiki/Free-market" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-market">free-market</a> ideology, bitcoin was invented in 2008 when an unknown person published a <a href="/wiki/White_paper" title="White paper">white paper</a> under the pseudonym of <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Nakamoto" title="Satoshi Nakamoto">Satoshi Nakamoto</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-whoissn&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoissn-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Use of bitcoin as a <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> began in 2009,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NY2011&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY2011-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with the release of its <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source implementation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 1">&#58;&#8202;ch. 1&#8202;</span></sup> From 2021 to 2025, <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_in_El_Salvador" title="Bitcoin in El Salvador">El Salvador adopted it as legal tender currency before revoking it</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BTCSVSept7FT&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTCSVSept7FT-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-El&#95;Salvador&#95;Abandons&#95;Bitcoin&#95;as&#95;Legal&#95;Tender&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Salvador_Abandons_Bitcoin_as_Legal_Tender-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bitcoin&#95;is&#95;no&#95;longer&#95;legal&#95;tender&#95;in&#95;El&#95;Salvador&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bitcoin_is_no_longer_legal_tender_in_El_Salvador-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As bitcoin is <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonymous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_and_crime" title="Cryptocurrency and crime">its use by criminals</a> has attracted the attention of regulators, leading to <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">its ban by several countries</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-SunYin2019&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunYin2019-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bitcoin works through the collaboration of computers, each of which acts as a <a href="/wiki/Node_(networking)" title="Node (networking)">node</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_network" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitcoin network">bitcoin network</a>. Each node maintains an independent copy of a public <a href="/wiki/Distributed_ledger" title="Distributed ledger">distributed ledger</a> of transactions, called a <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a>, without central oversight. Transactions are validated through the use of <a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">cryptography</a>, preventing one person from spending another person's bitcoin, as long as the owner of the bitcoin keeps certain sensitive data secret.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 5">&#58;&#8202;ch. 5&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Consensus_(computer_science)" title="Consensus (computer science)">Consensus</a> between nodes about the content of the blockchain is achieved using a <a href="/wiki/Computational_complexity" title="Computational complexity">computationally intensive</a> process based on <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_work" title="Proof of work">proof of work</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_mining" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitcoin mining">mining</a>, which is performed by purpose-built computers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 12">&#58;&#8202;ch. 12&#8202;</span></sup> Mining consumes large quantities of electricity and has been criticized for <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_bitcoin" title="Environmental impact of bitcoin">its environmental impact</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-4"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_bitcoin" title="History of bitcoin">History of bitcoin</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Background">Background</h3></div>
<p>Before bitcoin, several <a href="/wiki/Digital_cash" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital cash">digital cash technologies</a> were released, starting with <a href="/wiki/David_Chaum" title="David Chaum">David Chaum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ecash" title="Ecash">ecash</a> in the 1980s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The idea that solutions to computational puzzles could have some value was first proposed by cryptographers <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Dwork" title="Cynthia Dwork">Cynthia Dwork</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moni_Naor" title="Moni Naor">Moni Naor</a> in 1992.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The concept was <a href="/wiki/Multiple_discovery" title="Multiple discovery">independently rediscovered</a> by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Back" title="Adam Back">Adam Back</a> who developed <a href="/wiki/Hashcash" title="Hashcash">Hashcash</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Proof-of-work" class="mw-redirect" title="Proof-of-work">proof-of-work</a> scheme for <a href="/wiki/Anti-spam_techniques" title="Anti-spam techniques">spam control</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first proposals for distributed digital scarcity-based <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptocurrencies">cryptocurrencies</a> came from <a href="/wiki/Cypherpunk" title="Cypherpunk">cypherpunks</a> <a href="/wiki/Wei_Dai" title="Wei Dai">Wei Dai</a> (b-money) and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Szabo" title="Nick Szabo">Nick Szabo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bit_gold" class="mw-redirect" title="Bit gold">bit gold</a>) in 1998.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Hal_Finney_(cypherpunk)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hal Finney (cypherpunk)">Hal Finney</a> developed the first currency based on reusable proof of work.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These various attempts were not successful:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Chaum's concept required centralized control and no banks wanted to sign on, Hashcash had no protection against <a href="/wiki/Double-spending" title="Double-spending">double-spending</a>, while b-money and bit gold were not resistant to <a href="/wiki/Sybil_attack" title="Sybil attack">Sybil attacks</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2008–2009:_Creation"><span id="2008.E2.80.932009:_Creation"></span>2008–2009: Creation</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1316064257" /><table class="infobox" style="width: 258px; clear: right; float:right;margin:0 0 4px 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="font-size:115%">External image</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="text-align: left"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Searchtool.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="image icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/20px-Searchtool.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/40px-Searchtool.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.thetimes03jan2009.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/genesis-block-newspaper-bitcoin.jpg">Cover page of <i>The Times</i> 3 January 2009 showing the headline used in the genesis block</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The domain name <i>bitcoin.org</i> was registered on 18 August 2008.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 31 October 2008, a link to a <a href="/wiki/White_paper" title="White paper">white paper</a> authored by <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Nakamoto" title="Satoshi Nakamoto">Satoshi Nakamoto</a> titled <i>Bitcoin: A Peer-to-Peer Electronic Cash System</i> was posted to a cryptography mailing list.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nakamoto's identity remains unknown.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-whoissn&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoissn-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Narayanan" title="Arvind Narayanan">Arvind Narayanan</a>, all individual components of bitcoin originated in earlier academic literature.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nakamoto's innovation was their complex interplay resulting in the first decentralized, <a href="/wiki/Sybil_attack" title="Sybil attack">Sybil resistant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_fault" title="Byzantine fault">Byzantine fault</a> tolerant digital cash system, that would eventually be referred to as the first blockchain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-te20151031&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-te20151031-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nakamoto's paper was not <a href="/wiki/Peer_review" title="Peer review">peer reviewed</a> and was initially ignored by academics, who argued that it could not work.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Narayanan2017&#95;14-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Narayanan2017-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nakamoto released bitcoin as <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Humayun-2018&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humayun-2018-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 3 January 2009, the bitcoin network was created when Nakamoto mined the starting block of the chain, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Genesis_(blockchain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genesis (blockchain)">genesis block</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Wired:RFB&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wired:RFB-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Embedded in this block was the text "The Times 03/Jan/2009 Chancellor on brink of <a href="/wiki/2009_United_Kingdom_bank_rescue_package" title="2009 United Kingdom bank rescue package">second bailout for banks</a>", which is the date and headline of an issue of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> newspaper.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NY2011&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY2011-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nine days later, Hal Finney received the first bitcoin transaction: ten bitcoins from Nakamoto.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Wei Dai and Nick Szabo were also early supporters.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Wired:RFB&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wired:RFB-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On May 22, 2010, the first known <a href="/wiki/Financial_transaction" title="Financial transaction">commercial transaction</a> using bitcoin occurred when programmer Laszlo Hanyecz bought two <a href="/wiki/Papa_John%27s" title="Papa John&#39;s">Papa John's</a> pizzas for ₿10,000, in what would later be celebrated as "Bitcoin Pizza Day".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Satoshi tasked Finnish developer and early Bitcoin contributor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martti_Malmi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Martti Malmi (page does not exist)">Martti Malmi</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fi.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martti_Malmi" class="extiw" title="fi:Martti Malmi">fi</a>&#93;</span> with creating content for the bitcoin.org website.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-DominicFrisby2014&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DominicFrisby2014-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2010–2012:_Early_growth"><span id="2010.E2.80.932012:_Early_growth"></span>2010–2012: Early growth</h3></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Blockchain#Blockchain_analysis" title="Blockchain">Blockchain analysts</a> estimate that Nakamoto had mined about one million bitcoins<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> before disappearing in 2010 when he handed the network alert key and control of the <a href="/wiki/Software_repository" title="Software repository">code repository</a> over to <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Andresen" title="Gavin Andresen">Gavin Andresen</a>. Andresen later became lead developer at the <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Foundation" title="Bitcoin Foundation">Bitcoin Foundation</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/List_of_bitcoin_organizations" title="List of bitcoin organizations">organization</a> founded in September 2012 to promote bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After early "<a href="/wiki/Proof-of-concept" class="mw-redirect" title="Proof-of-concept">proof-of-concept</a>" transactions, the first major users of bitcoin were <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">black markets</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Dark_web" title="Dark web">dark web</a> <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road_(marketplace)" title="Silk Road (marketplace)">Silk Road</a>. During its 30 months of existence, beginning in February 2011, Silk Road exclusively accepted bitcoins as payment, transacting ₿9.9&#160;million, worth about $214&#160;million.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 222">&#58;&#8202;222&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2013–2014:_First_regulatory_actions"><span id="2013.E2.80.932014:_First_regulatory_actions"></span>2013–2014: First regulatory actions</h3></div>
<p>In March 2013, the US <a href="/wiki/Financial_Crimes_Enforcement_Network" title="Financial Crimes Enforcement Network">Financial Crimes Enforcement Network</a> (FinCEN) established regulatory guidelines for "decentralized virtual currencies" such as bitcoin, classifying American bitcoin miners who sell their generated bitcoins as <a href="/wiki/Money_services_business" title="Money services business">money services businesses</a>, subject to registration and other legal obligations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2013, US authorities seized the unregistered <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_exchange" title="Cryptocurrency exchange">exchange</a> <a href="/wiki/Mt._Gox" title="Mt. Gox">Mt. Gox</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In June 2013, the US <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a> seized ₿11.02 from an individual attempting to use them to purchase illicit drugs. This marked the first time a government agency had seized bitcoins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The FBI seized about ₿30,000 in October 2013 from Silk Road, following the arrest of its founder <a href="/wiki/Ross_Ulbricht" title="Ross Ulbricht">Ross Ulbricht</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2013, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Bank_of_China" title="People&#39;s Bank of China">People's Bank of China</a> prohibited Chinese financial institutions from using bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After the announcement, the value of bitcoin dropped,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a> no longer accepted bitcoins for certain services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Buying real-world goods with any virtual currency had been illegal in China since at least 2009.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2015–2019"><span id="2015.E2.80.932019"></span>2015–2019</h3></div>
<p>Research produced by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> estimated that in 2017, there were 2.9 to 5.8 million unique users using a <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_wallet" title="Cryptocurrency wallet">cryptocurrency wallet</a>, most of them using bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2017, the <a href="/wiki/SegWit" title="SegWit">SegWit</a> software upgrade was activated. Segwit was intended to support the <a href="/wiki/Lightning_Network" title="Lightning Network">Lightning Network</a> as well as improve <a href="/wiki/Scalability" title="Scalability">scalability</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> SegWit opponents, who supported larger blocks as a scalability solution, <a href="/wiki/Fork_(blockchain)" title="Fork (blockchain)">forked</a> to create <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Cash" title="Bitcoin Cash">Bitcoin Cash</a>, one of many <a href="/wiki/List_of_bitcoin_forks" title="List of bitcoin forks">forks of bitcoin</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2017, the first <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> on bitcoin was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Mercantile_Exchange" title="Chicago Mercantile Exchange">Chicago Mercantile Exchange</a> (CME).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2018, the price crashed after China imposed a complete ban on bitcoin trading.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The percentage of bitcoin trading in the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">renminbi</a> fell from over 90% in September 2017 to less than 1% in June 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the same year, bitcoin prices were negatively affected by several hacks or thefts from cryptocurrency exchanges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2020–present"><span id="2020.E2.80.93present"></span>2020–present</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bitcoin_Price.webp" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bitcoin_Price.webp/250px-Bitcoin_Price.webp.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="85" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bitcoin_Price.webp/500px-Bitcoin_Price.webp.png 2x" data-file-width="4827" data-file-height="1644" /></a><figcaption><div class="center"><b>Bitcoin price</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div> December 1, 2014 – <br /> December 4, 2024</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2020, some major companies and institutions started to acquire bitcoin: <a href="/wiki/MicroStrategy" title="MicroStrategy">MicroStrategy</a> invested $250 million in bitcoin as a <a href="/wiki/Treasury_management" title="Treasury management">treasury reserve asset</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Square,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Square, Inc.">Square, Inc.</a>, $50 million,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MassMutual" title="MassMutual">MassMutual</a>, $100 million.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 2020, <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> added support for bitcoin in the US.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2021, bitcoin's <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> reached $1 trillion for the first time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Taproot_(fork)" class="mw-redirect" title="Taproot (fork)">Taproot</a> <a href="/wiki/Soft-fork" class="mw-redirect" title="Soft-fork">soft-fork</a> upgrade was activated, adding support for <a href="/wiki/Schnorr_signature" title="Schnorr signature">Schnorr signatures</a>, improved functionality of <a href="/wiki/Smart_contract" title="Smart contract">smart contracts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lightning_Network" title="Lightning Network">Lightning Network</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before, bitcoin only used a custom <a href="/wiki/Elliptic_curve_cryptography" class="mw-redirect" title="Elliptic curve cryptography">elliptic curve</a> with the <a href="/wiki/ECDSA" class="mw-redirect" title="ECDSA">ECDSA</a> algorithm to produce <a href="/wiki/Digital_signature" title="Digital signature">signatures</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 101">&#58;&#8202;101&#8202;</span></sup> In September 2021, bitcoin became <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> currency <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_in_El_Salvador" title="Bitcoin in El Salvador">in El Salvador</a>, alongside the US dollar.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BTCSVSept7FT&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTCSVSept7FT-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2021, the first bitcoin futures <a href="/wiki/Exchange-traded_fund" title="Exchange-traded fund">exchange-traded fund</a> (ETF), called BITO, from <a href="/wiki/ProShares" title="ProShares">ProShares</a> was approved by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">SEC</a> and listed on the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Mercantile_Exchange" title="Chicago Mercantile Exchange">CME</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2022, during the <a href="/wiki/Canada_convoy_protest" title="Canada convoy protest">Canadian trucker protests</a> opposing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_vaccine_misinformation_and_hesitancy" title="COVID-19 vaccine misinformation and hesitancy">COVID-19 vaccine mandates</a>, organizers turned to bitcoin to receive donations after traditional financial platforms restricted access to funding.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Proponents highlighted bitcoin's use as a tool for fundraising in situations where access to conventional financial systems may be restricted.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May and June 2022, the bitcoin price fell following the collapses of <a href="/wiki/Terra_(blockchain)" title="Terra (blockchain)">TerraUSD</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Stablecoin" title="Stablecoin">stablecoin</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Celsius_Network" title="Celsius Network">Celsius Network</a>, a cryptocurrency loan company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, ordinals—<a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">non-fungible tokens</a> (NFTs)—on bitcoin, went live.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of June 2023, River Financial estimated that bitcoin had 81.7 million users, about 1% of the global population.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2024, the first 11 US <a href="/wiki/Spot_market" title="Spot market">spot</a> bitcoin <a href="/wiki/Exchange-traded_fund" title="Exchange-traded fund">ETFs</a> began trading, offering direct exposure to bitcoin for the first time on American stock exchanges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In December 2024, bitcoin price reached $100,000 for the first time, as US president-elect <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> promised to make the US the "crypto capital of the planet" and to stockpile bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The same month, <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a>, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Asset_manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Asset manager">asset manager</a>, recommended investors to allocate up to 2% of their <a href="/wiki/Portfolio_(finance)" title="Portfolio (finance)">portfolio</a> to bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2025, the Salvadoran government continues to describe Bitcoin as legal tender under the 2021 Bitcoin Law; however, a January 2025 reform removed obligations for businesses and the government to accept it, so many analysts regard its legal-tender status as effectively ended in practice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-El&#95;Salvador&#95;Abandons&#95;Bitcoin&#95;as&#95;Legal&#95;Tender&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Salvador_Abandons_Bitcoin_as_Legal_Tender-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bitcoin&#95;is&#95;no&#95;longer&#95;legal&#95;tender&#95;in&#95;El&#95;Salvador&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bitcoin_is_no_longer_legal_tender_in_El_Salvador-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In March 2025, <a href="/wiki/President_Trump" class="mw-redirect" title="President Trump">President Trump</a> signed an <a href="/wiki/Executive_order_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive order (United States)">executive order</a> to establish a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bitcoin_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic bitcoin reserve">strategic bitcoin reserve</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that year, some U.S. states, such as <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> also instituted strategic bitcoin reserves,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Bank" title="Czech National Bank">Czech National Bank</a> bought less than €1 million in a "test portfolio".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Design">Design</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_protocol" title="Bitcoin protocol">Bitcoin protocol</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Units_and_divisibility">Units and divisibility</h3></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:188px;max-width:188px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bitcoin_old.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8f/Bitcoin_old.png" decoding="async" width="90" height="90" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bitcoin.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bitcoin.png/120px-Bitcoin.png" decoding="async" width="90" height="89" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bitcoin.png/250px-Bitcoin.png 2x" data-file-width="530" data-file-height="526" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Bitcoin logos made by Satoshi Nakamoto in 2009 (left) and 2010 (right).</div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Unit_of_account" title="Unit of account">unit of account</a> of the bitcoin system is the <i>bitcoin</i>. It is most commonly represented with the <a href="/wiki/Currency_symbol" title="Currency symbol">symbol</a> ₿ designed in 2010<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unicode-10&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicode-10-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Currency_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Currency code">currency code</a> BTC. However, the BTC code does not conform to <a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> as BT is the country code of Bhutan,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ssrn.3383734&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssrn.3383734-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and ISO 4217 requires the first letter used in global commodities to be 'X'.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ssrn.3383734&#95;72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssrn.3383734-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> XBT, a code that conforms to <a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">ISO 4217</a> though not officially part of it,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ssrn.3383734&#95;72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssrn.3383734-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is used by <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg L.P.</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>No uniform <a href="/wiki/Capitalization" title="Capitalization">capitalization</a> convention exists; some sources use <i>Bitcoin</i>, capitalized, to refer to the technology and <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">network</a>, and <i>bitcoin</i>, lowercase, for the unit of account.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Advanced_Learner%27s_Dictionary" title="Cambridge Advanced Learner&#39;s Dictionary">Cambridge Advanced Learner's Dictionary</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_Advanced_Learner%27s_Dictionary" title="Oxford Advanced Learner&#39;s Dictionary">Oxford Advanced Learner's Dictionary</a></i> use the capitalized and lowercase variants without distinction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>One bitcoin is divisible to eight decimal places.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 5">&#58;&#8202;ch. 5&#8202;</span></sup> Units for smaller amounts of bitcoin are the millibitcoin (mBTC), equal to <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1154941027" /><span class="frac"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">1000</span></span> bitcoin, and the satoshi<sup id="cite&#95;ref-satoshi&#95;2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satoshi-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (sat), representing <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1154941027" /><span class="frac"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7008100000000000000♠"></span>100<span style="margin-left:.25em;">000</span><span style="margin-left:.25em;">000</span></span></span></span> (one hundred millionth) bitcoin, the smallest amount possible.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-satoshi&#95;unit&#95;3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satoshi_unit-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 100,000 satoshis are one mBTC.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Blockchain">Blockchain</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Blockchain#Structure_and_design" title="Blockchain">Blockchain §&#160;Structure and design</a></div>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Decentralization" title="Decentralization">decentralized</a> system, bitcoin operates without a central authority or single administrator,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gervais2014&#95;78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gervais2014-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> so that anyone can create a new bitcoin address and transact without needing any approval.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: ch. 1">&#58;&#8202;ch. 1&#8202;</span></sup> This is accomplished through a specialized <a href="/wiki/Distributed_ledger" title="Distributed ledger">distributed ledger</a> called a <i><a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a></i> that records bitcoin transactions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The blockchain is implemented as an ordered list of <i>blocks</i>. Each block contains a <a href="/wiki/SHA-256" class="mw-redirect" title="SHA-256">SHA-256</a> <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_hash_function" title="Cryptographic hash function">hash</a> of the previous block,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> chaining them in chronological order.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 7">&#58;&#8202;ch. 7&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The blockchain is maintained by a <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 215–219">&#58;&#8202;215–219&#8202;</span></sup> Individual blocks, public addresses, and transactions within blocks are public information, and can be examined using a blockchain explorer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nodes validate and broadcast transactions, each maintaining a copy of the blockchain for ownership verification.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A new block is created every 10 minutes on average, updating the blockchain across all nodes without central oversight. This process tracks bitcoin spending, ensuring each bitcoin is <a href="/wiki/Double-spending" title="Double-spending">spent only once</a>. Unlike a traditional ledger that tracks physical currency, bitcoins exist digitally as <a href="/wiki/Unspent_outputs_of_transactions" class="mw-redirect" title="Unspent outputs of transactions">unspent outputs of transactions</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 5">&#58;&#8202;ch. 5&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Addresses_and_transactions">Addresses and transactions</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bitcoin_Transaction_Visual.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bitcoin_Transaction_Visual.svg/250px-Bitcoin_Transaction_Visual.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bitcoin_Transaction_Visual.svg/500px-Bitcoin_Transaction_Visual.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="227" /></a><figcaption>Simplified chain of ownership. In practice, a transaction can have more than one input and more than one output.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconOfBTC&#95;82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconOfBTC-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In the blockchain, bitcoins are linked to specific <a href="/wiki/String_(computer_science)" title="String (computer science)">strings</a> called addresses. Most often, an address encodes a <a href="/wiki/Hash_(cryptography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hash (cryptography)">hash</a> of a single <a href="/wiki/Public_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Public key">public key</a>. Creating such an address involves generating a random private key and then computing the corresponding address. This process is almost instant, but the reverse (finding the private key for a given address) is nearly impossible.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 4">&#58;&#8202;ch. 4&#8202;</span></sup> Publishing such a bitcoin address does not risk its private key, and it is extremely unlikely to accidentally generate a used key with funds. To use bitcoins, owners need their private key to <a href="/wiki/Digital_signature" title="Digital signature">digitally sign</a> transactions, which are verified by the network using the public key, keeping the private key secret.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 5">&#58;&#8202;ch. 5&#8202;</span></sup> An address may encode the hash of a bitcoin script that specifies more complex requirements to spend the funds. One common example is "multisig", in which multiple distinct private keys must mutually sign any transaction that attempts to spend the funds.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 7">&#58;&#8202;ch. 7&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>Bitcoin transactions use a <a href="/wiki/Forth_(programming_language)" title="Forth (programming language)">Forth</a>-like <a href="/wiki/Scripting_language" title="Scripting language">scripting language</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: ch. 5">&#58;&#8202;ch. 5&#8202;</span></sup> involving one or more inputs and outputs. When sending bitcoins, a user specifies the recipients' addresses and the amount for each output. This allows sending bitcoins to several recipients in a single transaction. To prevent double-spending, each input must refer to a previous unspent output in the blockchain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconOfBTC&#95;82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconOfBTC-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Using multiple inputs is similar to using multiple coins in a cash transaction. As in a cash transaction, the sum of inputs can exceed the intended sum of payments. In such a case, an additional output can return the change back to the payer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconOfBTC&#95;82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconOfBTC-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Unallocated input satoshis in the transaction become the transaction fee.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconOfBTC&#95;82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconOfBTC-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Losing a private key means losing access to the bitcoins, with no other proof of ownership accepted by the <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_protocol" title="Bitcoin protocol">protocol</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For instance, in 2013, a user lost ₿7,500, valued at US$7.5 million, by accidentally discarding a <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk_drive" title="Hard disk drive">hard drive</a> with the private key.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is estimated that around 20% of all bitcoins are lost.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The private key must also be kept secret as its exposure, such as through a <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breach</a>, can lead to theft of the associated bitcoins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 10">&#58;&#8202;ch. 10&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of December&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, approximately ₿980,000 had been stolen from <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_exchange" title="Cryptocurrency exchange">cryptocurrency exchanges</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mining">Mining</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_protocol#Mining" title="Bitcoin protocol">Bitcoin protocol §&#160;Mining</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Argo_Blockchain_Mirabel_Facility.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Argo_Blockchain_Mirabel_Facility.jpg/250px-Argo_Blockchain_Mirabel_Facility.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Argo_Blockchain_Mirabel_Facility.jpg/500px-Argo_Blockchain_Mirabel_Facility.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4600" data-file-height="3450" /></a><figcaption>Bitcoin mining <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">facility</a> with large amounts of mining hardware</figcaption></figure>
<p>Miners don't directly act as nodes, but do communicate with nodes. The mining process is primarily intended to prevent <a href="/wiki/Double-spending" title="Double-spending">double-spending</a> and get all nodes to agree on the content of the blockchain, but it also has desirable side-effects such as making it infeasible for adversaries to stifle valid transactions or alter the historical record of transactions, since doing so generally requires the adversary to have access to more mining power than the rest of the network combined.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 12">&#58;&#8202;ch. 12&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>The mining process in bitcoin involves maintaining the blockchain through computer <a href="/wiki/Processing_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Processing power">processing power</a>. Miners group and broadcast new transactions into blocks, which are then verified by the network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each block must contain a proof of work (PoW) to be accepted,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> involving finding a <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_nonce" title="Cryptographic nonce">nonce</a> number that, combined with the block content, produces a <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_hash" class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptographic hash">hash</a> numerically smaller than the network's <i>difficulty target</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup> This PoW is simple to verify but hard to generate, requiring many attempts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup> PoW forms the basis of bitcoin's <a href="/wiki/Consensus_(computer_science)" title="Consensus (computer science)">consensus mechanism</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mingxiao2017&#95;87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mingxiao2017-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The difficulty of generating a block is <a href="/wiki/Deterministic_algorithm" title="Deterministic algorithm">deterministically adjusted</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Hashrate" title="Hashrate">mining power on the network</a> by changing the difficulty target, which is recalibrated every 2,016 blocks (approximately two weeks) to maintain an average time of ten minutes between new blocks. The process requires significant computational power and specialized <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">hardware</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Miners who successfully create a new block with a valid nonce can collect transaction fees from the included transactions and a fixed reward in bitcoins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-bloombergvance111413&#95;89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergvance111413-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To claim this reward, a special transaction called a <i>coinbase</i> is included in the block, with the miner as the payee. All bitcoins in existence have been created through this type of transaction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup> This reward is halved every 210,000 blocks until ₿21&#160;million<sup id="cite&#95;ref-supply&#95;5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supply-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>b<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> have been issued in total, which is expected to occur around the year 2140. Afterward, miners will only earn from transaction fees. These fees are determined by the transaction's size and the amount of data stored, measured in satoshis per byte.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-EconOfBTC&#95;82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconOfBTC-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>The proof of work system and the chaining of blocks make blockchain modifications very difficult, as altering one block requires changing all subsequent blocks. As more blocks are added, modifying older blocks becomes increasingly challenging.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-econbc&#95;79-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econbc-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In case of disagreement, nodes trust the longest chain, which required the greatest amount of effort to produce.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mingxiao2017&#95;87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mingxiao2017-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To tamper or censor the ledger, one needs to control the majority of the global <a href="/wiki/Hashrate" title="Hashrate">hashrate</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mingxiao2017&#95;87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mingxiao2017-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The high cost required to reach this level of computational power <a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">secures</a> the bitcoin blockchain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mingxiao2017&#95;87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mingxiao2017-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_bitcoin_mining" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental impact of bitcoin mining">environmental impact of bitcoin mining</a> is controversial and has attracted the attention of regulators, <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">leading to restrictions or incentives in various jurisdictions</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Stoll2023&#95;92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stoll2023-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2025<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, a <a href="/wiki/Non-peer-reviewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-peer-reviewed">non-peer-reviewed</a> study by the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Centre_for_Alternative_Finance" title="Cambridge Centre for Alternative Finance">Cambridge Centre for Alternative Finance</a> (CCAF) estimated that bitcoin mining represented 0.5% of <a href="/wiki/World_energy_supply_and_consumption" title="World energy supply and consumption">global electricity consumption</a> and 0.08% of world <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>, comparable to Slovakia's emissions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> About half of the electricity used is generated through <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYT20220116&#95;94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT20220116-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Moreover, mining hardware's short lifespan results in <a href="/wiki/Electronic_waste" title="Electronic waste">electronic waste</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-deVries2021&#95;95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deVries2021-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2025, the US was the largest mining country with 38% of the global bitcoin mining market share, followed by Russia (16%) and China (14%, despite all cryptocurrency trading and mining being banned there in 2021).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Privacy_and_fungibility">Privacy and fungibility</h3></div>
<p>Bitcoin is <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonymous</a>, with funds linked to addresses, not real-world identities. While the owners of these addresses are not directly identified, all transactions are public on the blockchain. Patterns of use, like spending coins from multiple inputs, can hint at a common owner. Public data can sometimes be matched with known address owners.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_bitcoin_companies" title="List of bitcoin companies">Bitcoin exchanges</a> might also need to collect personal data as per legal requirements.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For enhanced <a href="/wiki/Privacy_and_blockchain" class="mw-redirect" title="Privacy and blockchain">privacy</a>, users can generate a new address for each transaction.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the bitcoin network, each bitcoin is treated equally, ensuring basic <a href="/wiki/Fungibility" title="Fungibility">fungibility</a>. However, users and applications can choose to differentiate between bitcoins. While wallets and software treat all bitcoins the same, each bitcoin's transaction history is recorded on the blockchain. This public record allows for <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_analysis" title="Blockchain analysis">chain analysis</a>, where users can identify and potentially reject bitcoins from controversial sources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, in 2012, Mt. Gox froze accounts containing bitcoins identified as stolen.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Wallets">Wallets</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For broader coverage of this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_wallet" title="Cryptocurrency wallet">Cryptocurrency wallet</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tnone center"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:592px;max-width:592px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:163px;max-width:163px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:111px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bitcoin-core-v0.10.0.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bitcoin-core-v0.10.0.png/250px-Bitcoin-core-v0.10.0.png" decoding="async" width="161" height="111" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bitcoin-core-v0.10.0.png/330px-Bitcoin-core-v0.10.0.png 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="590" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Screenshot of <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Core" title="Bitcoin Core">Bitcoin Core</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:111px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sample_Bitcoin_paper_wallet.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Sample_Bitcoin_paper_wallet.png/250px-Sample_Bitcoin_paper_wallet.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Sample_Bitcoin_paper_wallet.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="203" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">A paper wallet with the address as a <a href="/wiki/QR_code" title="QR code">QR code</a> while the private key is hidden</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:201px;max-width:201px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:111px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:10elqpi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/10elqpi.jpg/250px-10elqpi.jpg" decoding="async" width="199" height="112" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/10elqpi.jpg/500px-10elqpi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="900" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">A hardware wallet which processes bitcoin transactions without exposing private keys</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Bitcoin wallets were the first <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_wallet" title="Cryptocurrency wallet">cryptocurrency wallets</a>, enabling users to store the information necessary to transact bitcoins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: ch. 1, glossary">&#58;&#8202;ch. 1, glossary&#8202;</span></sup> The first wallet program, simply named <i>Bitcoin</i>, and sometimes referred to as the <i>Satoshi client</i>, was released in 2009 by Nakamoto as <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Humayun-2018&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humayun-2018-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Core" title="Bitcoin Core">Bitcoin Core</a> is among the best known <a href="/wiki/Client_(computing)" title="Client (computing)">clients</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">Forks</a> of Bitcoin Core exist such as <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Unlimited" title="Bitcoin Unlimited">Bitcoin Unlimited</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Wallets can be full clients, with a full copy of the blockchain to check the validity of mined blocks,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: ch. 1">&#58;&#8202;ch. 1&#8202;</span></sup> or lightweight clients, just to send and receive transactions without a local copy of the entire blockchain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Third-party internet services, called online wallets or <a href="/wiki/Digital_wallet" title="Digital wallet">hot wallets</a>, store users' credentials on their servers, making them susceptible of hacks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cold_wallet" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold wallet">Cold storage</a> protects bitcoins from such hacks by keeping private keys offline, either through specialized hardware wallets or paper printouts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 4">&#58;&#8202;ch. 4&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Scalability_and_decentralization_challenges">Scalability and decentralization challenges</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_scalability_problem" title="Bitcoin scalability problem">Bitcoin scalability problem</a></div>
<p>Nakamoto limited the block size to one <a href="/wiki/Megabyte" title="Megabyte">megabyte</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The limited block size and frequency can lead to delayed processing of transactions, increased fees and a bitcoin scalability problem.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lightning_Network" title="Lightning Network">Lightning Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_layer" title="Abstraction layer">second-layer</a> <a href="/wiki/Routing" title="Routing">routing</a> network, is a potential scaling solution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Antonopoulos2014&#95;8-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antonopoulos2014-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: ch. 8">&#58;&#8202;ch. 8&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>Research shows a trend towards centralization in bitcoin as miners join <a href="/wiki/Mining_pool" title="Mining pool">pools</a> for stable income.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 215, 219–222">&#58;&#8202;215,&#8202;219–222&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 3">&#58;&#8202;3&#8202;</span></sup> If a single miner or pool controls more than 50% of the <a href="/wiki/Hashrate" title="Hashrate">hashing power</a>, it would allow them to censor transactions and double-spend coins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gervais2014&#95;78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gervais2014-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2014, mining pool <a href="/wiki/Ghash.io" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghash.io">Ghash.io</a> reached 51% mining power, causing safety concerns, but later voluntarily capped its power at 39.99% for the benefit of the whole network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A few entities also dominate other parts of the ecosystem such as the client software, online wallets, and simplified payment verification (SPV) clients.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gervais2014&#95;78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gervais2014-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economics_and_usage">Economics and usage</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_bitcoin" title="Economics of bitcoin">Economics of bitcoin</a></div>
