<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bitcoin's_theoretical_roots_and_ideology"><span id="Bitcoin.27s_theoretical_roots_and_ideology"></span>Bitcoin's theoretical roots and ideology</h3></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, the decentralization of money offered by bitcoin has its theoretical roots in the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_school_of_economics" title="Austrian school of economics">Austrian school of economics</a>, especially with <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Denationalisation_of_Money" title="The Denationalisation of Money">The Denationalisation of Money</a></i>, in which he advocates a complete <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> in the production, distribution and management of money to end the monopoly of <a href="/wiki/Central_banks" class="mw-redirect" title="Central banks">central banks</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 22">&#58;&#8202;22&#8202;</span></sup> Sociologist <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Dodd" title="Nigel Dodd">Nigel Dodd</a> argues that the essence of the bitcoin ideology is to remove money from social, as well as governmental, control.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> describes bitcoin as "a <a href="/wiki/Techno-anarchist" class="mw-redirect" title="Techno-anarchist">techno-anarchist</a> project to create an online version of cash, a way for people to transact without the possibility of interference from malicious governments or banks".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30082018Economist&#95;114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30082018Economist-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These philosophical ideas initially attracted <a href="/wiki/Libertarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Libertarian">libertarians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarchist">anarchists</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recognition_as_a_currency_and_legal_status">Recognition as a currency and legal status</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Legal_status_of_bitcoin.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Legal_status_of_bitcoin.svg/330px-Legal_status_of_bitcoin.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Legal_status_of_bitcoin.svg/960px-Legal_status_of_bitcoin.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2754" data-file-height="1398" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">Legal status of bitcoin</a> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#33cc66; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffd629; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;Restricted (some legal restrictions on the usage of bitcoin)</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ec6dd5; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;Contentious (interpretation of old laws, but bitcoin is not directly prohibited)</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff3333; color:black;-webkit-print-color-adjust: exact; print-color-adjust: exact;">&#160;</span>&#160;Prohibited (full or partial prohibition on the use of bitcoin)</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" /><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#b9b9b9; data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1333133064">.mw-parser-output .hlist dl,.mw-parser-output .hlist ol,.mw-parser-output .hlist ul{margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .hlist dd,.mw-parser-output </figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">Money</a> serves three purposes: a <a href="/wiki/Store_of_value" title="Store of value">store of value</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Medium_of_exchange" title="Medium of exchange">medium of exchange</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Unit_of_account" title="Unit of account">unit of account</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econ315&#95;116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ315-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to <i>The Economist</i> in 2014, bitcoin functions best as a medium of exchange.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-econ315&#95;116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ315-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2015, <i>The Economist</i> noted that bitcoins had three qualities useful in a currency: they are "hard to earn, limited in supply and easy to verify".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, a 2018 assessment by <i>The Economist</i> stated that cryptocurrencies met none of these three criteria.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30082018Economist&#95;114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30082018Economist-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Per some researchers, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, bitcoin functions more as a <a href="/wiki/Payment_system" title="Payment system">payment system</a> than as a currency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2014, economist <a href="/wiki/Robert_J._Shiller" title="Robert J. Shiller">Robert J. Shiller</a> wrote that bitcoin has potential as a unit of account for measuring the relative value of goods, as with Chile's <a href="/wiki/Unidad_de_Fomento" title="Unidad de Fomento">Unidad de Fomento</a>, but that "Bitcoin in its present form... doesn't really solve any sensible economic problem".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shiller&#95;118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shiller-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2017, François Velde, senior economist at the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Fed" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Fed">Chicago Fed</a>, described bitcoin as "unlikely by itself to replace monies in well-functioning monetary systems."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cryptocurrency_by_country_or_territory" title="Legality of cryptocurrency by country or territory">legal status of bitcoin</a> varies substantially from one jurisdiction to another. Because of its decentralized nature and its global presence, regulating bitcoin is difficult. However, the use of bitcoin can be criminalized, and shutting down exchanges and the peer-to-peer economy in a given country would constitute a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> ban.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_and_crime" title="Cryptocurrency and crime">use of bitcoin by criminals</a> has attracted the attention of financial regulators, legislative bodies, and law enforcement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nobel-prize winning economist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stiglitz" title="Joseph Stiglitz">Joseph Stiglitz</a> says that bitcoin's anonymity encourages <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> and other crimes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is the main justification behind bitcoin bans.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-SunYin2019&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunYin2019-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of November&#160;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, nine countries applied an absolute ban (Algeria, Bangladesh, China, Egypt, Iraq, Morocco, Nepal, Qatar, and Tunisia) while another 42 countries had an implicit ban.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LOC2021&#95;123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC2021-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Many things have changed since Nov 2021. (November 2023)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Use_for_payments">Use for payments</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Waag_Bitcoin.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/De_Waag_Bitcoin.jpg/250px-De_Waag_Bitcoin.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/De_Waag_Bitcoin.jpg/500px-De_Waag_Bitcoin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>Café in <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a> accepting Bitcoin</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to Harvard Professor <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Rogoff" title="Kenneth Rogoff">Kenneth Rogoff</a> as of 2025<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, bitcoin is rarely used in regular transactions with merchants, but is popular in the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a> and for criminal activities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RogoffEconomist&#95;124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RogoffEconomist-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-RogoffBloomberg&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RogoffBloomberg-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prices are not usually quoted in bitcoin and trades involve conversions into <a href="/wiki/Fiat_money" title="Fiat money">fiat</a> currencies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Commonly cited reasons for not using bitcoin include high costs, the inability to process <a href="/wiki/Chargeback" title="Chargeback">chargebacks</a>, high <a href="/wiki/Volatility_(finance)" title="Volatility (finance)">price volatility</a>, long transaction times, and <a href="/wiki/Transaction_cost" title="Transaction cost">transaction fees</a> (especially for small purchases).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FT08062018&#95;126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT08062018-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_News" title="Bloomberg News">Bloomberg</a></i> reported that bitcoin was being used for large-item purchases on the site <a href="/wiki/Overstock.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Overstock.com">Overstock.com</a> and for cross-border payments to <a href="/wiki/Freelancer" title="Freelancer">freelancers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there was little sign of bitcoin use in international <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> despite high fees charged by banks and <a href="/wiki/Western_Union" title="Western Union">Western Union</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-JEP&#95;31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JEP-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From September 2021 until January 2025, the <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Law" title="Bitcoin Law">Bitcoin Law</a> made bitcoin a <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> currency in <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, alongside the US dollar.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BTCSVSept7FT&#95;9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTCSVSept7FT-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The adoption had been criticized internationally and within El Salvador.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BTCSVSept7FT&#95;9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTCSVSept7FT-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2022, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) urged El Salvador to reverse its decision.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the use of <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_in_El_Salvador" title="Bitcoin in El Salvador">Bitcoin in El Salvador</a> remained low: 80% of businesses refused to accept it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2025, El Salvador's government revoked bitcoin's status as legal tender currency in order to comply with conditions set by the IMF for a loan. El Salvador still describes bitcoin as "legal tender", but its acceptance is no longer obligitory (as it is with the US dollar) and the El Salvador government no longer accepts bitcoin for payment of taxes or fees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-El&#95;Salvador&#95;Abandons&#95;Bitcoin&#95;as&#95;Legal&#95;Tender&#95;10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Salvador_Abandons_Bitcoin_as_Legal_Tender-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bitcoin&#95;is&#95;no&#95;longer&#95;legal&#95;tender&#95;in&#95;El&#95;Salvador&#95;11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bitcoin_is_no_longer_legal_tender_in_El_Salvador-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> (CAR) adopted bitcoin as legal tender alongside the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but repealed the reform one year later.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bitcoin is also used by some governments. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Iran" title="Government of Iran">Iranian government</a> initially opposed cryptocurrencies, but later began using them to circumvent <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctions against Iran">sanctions</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since 2020, Iran has required local bitcoin miners to sell bitcoin to the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Iran" title="Central Bank of Iran">Central Bank of Iran</a>, allowing the central bank to use it for imports.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-aawsat202011&#95;136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aawsat202011-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituent state">constituent states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local governments</a> also accept tax payments in bitcoin, including <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> in the US<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zug" title="Canton of Zug">Zug</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lugano" title="Lugano">Lugano</a> in Switzerland.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2023, the US government owned more than $5 billion worth of seized bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Use_for_investment_and_status_as_an_economic_bubble">Use for investment and status as an economic bubble</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_bubble" title="Cryptocurrency bubble">Cryptocurrency bubble</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_Bitcoin_reserves.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/El_Salvador_Bitcoin_reserves.png/250px-El_Salvador_Bitcoin_reserves.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="344" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/El_Salvador_Bitcoin_reserves.png/500px-El_Salvador_Bitcoin_reserves.png 2x" data-file-width="588" data-file-height="809" /></a><figcaption>Government website with El Salvador reserves</figcaption></figure>
<p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the overwhelming majority of bitcoin transactions took place on <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency_exchange" title="Cryptocurrency exchange">cryptocurrency exchanges</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FT08062018&#95;126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT08062018-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since 2014, regulated bitcoin funds also allow <a href="/wiki/Market_exposure" class="mw-redirect" title="Market exposure">exposure</a> to the asset or to <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> as an investment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bitcoin is used as a <a href="/wiki/Store_of_value" title="Store of value">store of value</a>:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> individuals and companies such as the <a href="/wiki/Winklevoss_Capital_Management" title="Winklevoss Capital Management">Winklevoss twins</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>'s companies <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla</a> have each bought and sold hundreds of millions of dollars worth of bitcoin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bitcoin wealth is highly concentrated, with 0.01% holding 27% of in-circulation currency, as of 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of March 2025, El Salvador had $550 million worth of bitcoin in its <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves">international reserves</a>, about 6,102 coins.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Bitcoin, along with other cryptocurrencies, has been described as an <a href="/wiki/Economic_bubble" title="Economic bubble">economic bubble</a> by several economists, including <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Prize in Economics</a> laureates, such as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stiglitz" title="Joseph Stiglitz">Joseph Stiglitz</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Stiglitz&#95;152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stiglitz-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Heckman" title="James Heckman">James Heckman</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4Nobels&#95;153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Nobels-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Krugman" title="Paul Krugman">Paul Krugman</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Krugman&#95;154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krugman-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another recipient of the prize, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Shiller" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Shiller">Robert Shiller</a>, argues that bitcoin is rather a <a href="/wiki/Fad" title="Fad">fad</a> that may become an <a href="/wiki/Asset_classes" title="Asset classes">asset class</a>. He describes its price growth as an "epidemic", driven by <a href="/wiki/Social_contagion" title="Social contagion">contagious narratives</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Tirole" title="Jean Tirole">Jean Tirole</a>, also Nobel laureate, described bitcoin as a "pure bubble" as its <a href="/wiki/Intrinsic_value_(finance)" title="Intrinsic value (finance)">intrinsic value</a> is zero. According to him, some bubbles are long-lasting such as gold and fiat currencies, and it is impossible to predict whether bitcoin would implode like other financial bubbles or become an alternative to gold.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The same year, <a href="/wiki/Chair_of_the_Federal_Reserve" title="Chair of the Federal Reserve">Federal Reserve Chair</a> <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Powell" title="Jerome Powell">Jerome Powell</a> described bitcoin as a digital competitor to gold but not to the dollar as he argued it is a highly volatile <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculative</a> asset not used as a form of payment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2025, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Rogoff" title="Kenneth Rogoff">Kenneth Rogoff</a> claimed that Krugman was wrong and that Bitcoin had value as it is competing with the dollar to become the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Means of exchange">means of exchange</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">underground economy</a> which represents 20% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RogoffEconomist&#95;124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RogoffEconomist-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-RogoffBloomberg&#95;125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RogoffBloomberg-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Rogoff, bitcoin is "the ideal currency for a more fragmented and uncertain global landscape" and it could become appealing to <a href="/wiki/Emerging_market" title="Emerging market">emerging-market</a> central banks as a "politically neutral" <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve</a> <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">currency</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2025, the nominee for the Chair of the Federal Reserve, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Warsh" title="Kevin Warsh">Kevin Warsh</a>, described Bitcoin as the "new gold."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to research published in the <i><a href="/wiki/International_Review_of_Financial_Analysis" title="International Review of Financial Analysis">International Review of Financial Analysis</a></i> in 2018, bitcoin as an asset is highly volatile and does not behave like any other conventional asset.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to one 2022 analysis published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Journal_of_Alternative_Investments" class="mw-redirect" title="The Journal of Alternative Investments">The Journal of Alternative Investments</a></i>, bitcoin was less volatile than <a href="/wiki/Price_of_oil" title="Price of oil">oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_as_an_investment" title="Silver as an investment">silver</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Treasury_security" title="United States Treasury security">US Treasuries</a>, and 190 stocks in the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> during and after the <a href="/wiki/2020_stock_market_crash" title="2020 stock market crash">2020 stock market crash</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The term <i lang="en"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hodl#English" class="extiw" title="wikt:hodl">hodl</a></i> was created in December 2013 for <a href="/wiki/Buy_and_hold" title="Buy and hold">holding</a> bitcoin rather than selling it during periods of volatility.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, economist <a href="/wiki/Nouriel_Roubini" title="Nouriel Roubini">Nouriel Roubini</a> described bitcoin as a <a href="/wiki/Ponzi_scheme" title="Ponzi scheme">Ponzi scheme</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Eric_Posner" title="Eric Posner">Eric Posner</a> disagrees, however, as "a real Ponzi scheme takes fraud; bitcoin, by contrast, seems more like a collective <a href="/wiki/Delusion" title="Delusion">delusion</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2014 <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> report also concluded that bitcoin was not a deliberate Ponzi scheme.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Market_characteristics">Market characteristics</h3></div>
<p>Bitcoin markets operate 24 hours a day, seven days a week, contrasting with traditional financial markets that have fixed trading hours. Bitcoin prices show much higher volatility and respond strongly to both regulatory changes and market events.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The volume of bitcoin trading can fluctuate considerably among various exchanges and geographic regions. The daily transaction volume of bitcoin across all exchanges typically reaches $50 billion as of 2025.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite&#95;note-ssrn.3383734-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ssrn.3383734_72-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ssrn.3383734_72-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ssrn.3383734_72-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFAlexanderImeraj2019" class="citation journal cs1">Alexander, Carol; Imeraj, Arben (2019). <span class="id-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ssrn.com/abstract=3383734">"Introducing the BITIX: The Bitcoin Fear Gauge"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/SSRN_Electronic_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="SSRN Electronic Journal">SSRN Electronic Journal</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.2139%2Fssrn.3383734">10.2139/ssrn.3383734</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://search.worldcat.org/issn/1556-5068">1556-5068</a>. <q>XBT satisfies the norm 'ISO 4217' by the International Organisation for Standardisation (ISO) as BTC goes against the name of Bhutan's currency. In general, transaction instruments that are not national currencies, like gold or silver, begin with an X. However, the symbol XBT is not officially recognised by ISO.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=SSRN+Electronic+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=Introducing+the+BITIX%3A+The+Bitcoin+Fear+Gauge&amp;rft.date=2019&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Adoi%2F10.2139%2Fssrn.3383734&amp;rft.issn=1556-5068&amp;rft.aulast=Alexander&amp;rft.aufirst=Carol&amp;rft.au=Imeraj%2C+Arben&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ssrn.com%2Fabstract%3D3383734&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABitcoin" class="Z3988"></span></span>
